# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`
- [ ] Provide reasoning for the localization

     1→{
     2→  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/dir.c"],

     4→  "confidence": 0.85,
     5→  "reasoning": "The bug is in fs/nfs/dir.c function nfs_lookup_revalidate at lines 1158-1161. When nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns an error (e.g., -512 from RPC call failure), the code treats any non-zero return value identically - it goes to out_zap_parent which clears parent directory caches and then falls through to out_bad, ultimately returning 0 (marking the dentry as invalid). This causes VFS to drop the dentry from cache. However, RPC errors (like -512 from network issues) should not automatically invalidate the dentry. Instead, they should be propagated to the caller or handled as transient failures. The issue is that the code does not distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC errors from the getattr() call (which are transient network failures). When autofs mount points depend on this dentry, marking it invalid causes the entire mount tree to be unmounted, even though the RPC failure is transient. The fix requires checking the error type from nfs_lookup_verify_inode and only going to out_zap_parent for specific errors that indicate parent directory changes, while propagating RPC errors to the caller instead of invalidating the dentry."
     6→}

84-assistanttext-
Perfect! My fault localization analysis is complete. Let me create a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I have successfully localized the NFS inode revalidation bug in the Linux kernel 4.1.15. The analysis involved:

### Methodology:
1. **Analyzed the bug report**: Root NFS with autofs mounts disappearing after mount expiration due to inode revalidation failures
2. **Traced error messages**: Found error path from `fs/nfs/proc.c` and `fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c` reporting "NFS reply getattr: -512"
3. **Followed error propagation**: Traced error through `__nfs_revalidate_inode` → `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` → `nfs_lookup_revalidate`
4. **Identified the root cause**: Improper error handling in `nfs_lookup_revalidate` function

### Key Findings:

**Buggy File**: `fs/nfs/dir.c`
**Buggy Function**: `nfs_lookup_revalidate` (lines 1158-1161)

**The Bug**: 
When `nfs_lookup_verify_inode()` returns any non-zero error (including RPC errors like -512), the code unconditionally goes to `out_zap_parent`, which invalidates the dentry by returning 0 to the VFS layer. This causes the VFS to drop the dentry from cache.

**The Problem**: 
RPC errors (like -512) are transient network failures, not indications that the dentry is invalid. The current code treats them identically to parent directory change errors, causing:
- The dentry to be marked invalid
- The VFS to drop it from cache
- For autofs mount points, this unmounts the entire mount tree

**Why It's a Regression**: 
The code doesn't distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC/network errors (which should be propagated or retried).

The result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` with a confidence level of 0.85.

When nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns an error (e.g., -512 from RPC call failure), the code treats any non-zero return value identically - it goes to out_zap_parent which clears parent directory caches and then falls through to out_bad, ultimately returning 0 (marking the dentry as invalid). This causes VFS to drop the dentry from cache. However, RPC errors (like -512 from network issues) should not automatically invalidate the dentry. Instead, they should be propagated to the caller or handled as transient failures. The issue is that the code does not distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC errors from the getattr() call (which are transient network failures). When autofs mount points depend on this dentry, marking it invalid causes the entire mount tree to be unmounted, even though the RPC failure is transient. The fix requires checking the error type from nfs_lookup_verify_inode and only going to out_zap_parent for specific errors that indicate parent directory changes, while propagating RPC errors to the caller instead of invalidating the dentry.\"\n}\n",

When nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns an error (e.g., -512 from RPC call failure), the code treats any non-zero return value identically - it goes to out_zap_parent which clears parent directory caches and then falls through to out_bad, ultimately returning 0 (marking the dentry as invalid). This causes VFS to drop the dentry from cache. However, RPC errors (like -512 from network issues) should not automatically invalidate the dentry. Instead, they should be propagated to the caller or handled as transient failures. The issue is that the code does not distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC errors from the getattr() call (which are transient network failures). When autofs mount points depend on this dentry, marking it invalid causes the entire mount tree to be unmounted, even though the RPC failure is transient. The fix requires checking the error type from nfs_lookup_verify_inode and only going to out_zap_parent for specific errors that indicate parent directory changes, while propagating RPC errors to the caller instead of invalidating the dentry.\"\n}\n",

  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/dir.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["nfs_lookup_revalidate"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The bug is in fs/nfs/dir.c function nfs_lookup_revalidate at lines 1158-1161. When nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns an error (e.g., -512 from RPC call failure), the code treats any non-zero return value identically - it goes to out_zap_parent which clears parent directory caches and then falls through to out_bad, ultimately returning 0 (marking the dentry as invalid). This causes VFS to drop the dentry from cache. However, RPC errors (like -512 from network issues) should not automatically invalidate the dentry. Instead, they should be propagated to the caller or handled as transient failures. The issue is that the code does not distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC errors from the getattr() call (which are transient network failures). When autofs mount points depend on this dentry, marking it invalid causes the entire mount tree to be unmounted, even though the RPC failure is transient. The fix requires checking the error type from nfs_lookup_verify_inode and only going to out_zap_parent for specific errors that indicate parent directory changes, while propagating RPC errors to the caller instead of invalidating the dentry."
}
